     <p>
      <b>
       Benjamin Solomon
      </b>
      "
      <b>
       Ben
      </b>
      "
      <b>
       Carson, Sr.
      </b>
      (born September 18, 1951) is an American
      <a href="/wiki/Politician" title="Politician">
       politician
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Author" title="Author">
       author
      </a>
      , and retired
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">
       Johns Hopkins
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">
       neurosurgeon
      </a>
      . He was the first surgeon to successfully separate
      <a href="/wiki/Craniopagus_twins" title="Craniopagus twins">
       conjoined twins joined at the head
      </a>
      . In 2008 he was awarded the
      <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">
       Presidential Medal of Freedom
      </a>
      by President
      <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">
       George W. Bush
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      After delivering a widely publicized speech at the 2013
      <a href="/wiki/National_Prayer_Breakfast" title="National Prayer Breakfast">
       National Prayer Breakfast
      </a>
      , he became a popular
      <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">
       conservative
      </a>
      figure in political media for his views on social and political issues.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carson
      <a href="/wiki/Ben_Carson_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Ben Carson presidential campaign, 2016">
       is running for
      </a>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2016">
       Republican nomination
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
       President of the United States
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">
       2016 election
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peoples_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Peoples-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">
       Early life
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Carson was born in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan" title="Detroit, Michigan">
       Detroit, Michigan
      </a>
      , the son of Sonya (ne Copeland) and Robert Solomon Carson, a
      <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">
       Seventh-day Adventist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">
       minister
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtref1_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-rtref1-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both his parents came from rural Georgia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rtref1_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-rtref1-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A DNA test on the television series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/African_American_Lives" title="African American Lives">
        African American Lives
       </a>
      </i>
      stated that he is of 80% African and 20% European ancestry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His parents divorced when he was eight, and he and his ten-year-old brother Curtis were raised by their mother.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In his book
      <i>
       Gifted Hands
      </i>
      , Carson relates that in his youth, he had a violent temper. Once, while in the ninth grade, he nearly stabbed a friend during a fight over a radio station, instead breaking the knife blade.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fritze_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fritze-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After this incident, he began reading the
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Proverbs" title="Book of Proverbs">
       Book of Proverbs
      </a>
      , applying verses on anger and thereafter "never had another problem with temper".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson attended
      <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_High_School_(Michigan)" title="Southwestern High School (Michigan)">
       Southwestern High School
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Detroit" title="Southwest Detroit">
       Southwest Detroit
      </a>
      where he excelled in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JROTC" title="JROTC">
       JROTC
      </a>
      . He quickly rose in rank and was offered an appointment to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Point" title="West Point">
       West Point
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Foster-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson graduated from
      <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">
       Yale University
      </a>
      , where he majored in
      <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">
       psychology
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He received his
      <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">
       M.D.
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">
       University of Michigan
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan_Medical_School" title="University of Michigan Medical School">
       Medical School
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He completed his residency in neurosurgery at Johns Hopkins Hospital in Baltimore.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_career">
       Medical career
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson,_MD.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="1418" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg/170px-Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg/255px-Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg/340px-Ben_Carson%2C_MD.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson,_MD.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Ben Carson in 2013
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Carson was a professor of
      <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">
       neurosurgery
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">
       oncology
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">
       plastic surgery
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">
       pediatrics
      </a>
      , and he was the director of pediatric neurosurgery at
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">
       Johns Hopkins Hospital
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At 33, he became the youngest major division director in the hospital's history as director of pediatric neurosurgery. He was also a co-director of the Johns Hopkins Craniofacial Center.
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson specialized in traumatic brain injuries, brain and spinal cord tumors,
      <a href="/wiki/Achondroplasia" title="Achondroplasia">
       achondroplasia
      </a>
      , neurological and congenital disorders,
      <a href="/wiki/Craniosynostosis" title="Craniosynostosis">
       craniosynostosis
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">
       epilepsy
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Trigeminal_neuralgia" title="Trigeminal neuralgia">
       trigeminal neuralgia
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson believes his
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand%E2%80%93eye_coordination" title="Handeye coordination">
       handeye coordination
      </a>
      and three-dimensional reasoning made him a gifted surgeon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennState_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PennState-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After medical school, he became a neurosurgery resident at Johns Hopkins Hospital. He began his career as a neurosurgeon, but also developed an interest in
      <a href="/wiki/Pediatrics" title="Pediatrics">
       pediatrics
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennState_16-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-PennState-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1987, Carson successfully separated
      <a href="/wiki/Conjoined_twins" title="Conjoined twins">
       conjoined twins
      </a>
      , the Binder twins, who had been joined at the back of the head (
      <a href="/wiki/Craniopagus_twins" title="Craniopagus twins">
       craniopagus twins
      </a>
      ). The 70-member surgical team, led by Carson, worked for 22 hours. Both twins survived.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson figured in the revival of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hemispherectomy" title="Hemispherectomy">
       hemispherectomy
      </a>
      , a drastic surgical procedure in which part or all of one hemisphere of the brain is removed to control severe pediatric
      <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">
       epilepsy
      </a>
      . He refined the procedure in the 1980s, encouraged by
      <a href="/wiki/John_M._Freeman_(neurologist)" title="John M. Freeman (neurologist)">
       John M. Freeman (neurologist)
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and performed it many times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson has served on the boards of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kellogg_Company" title="Kellogg Company">
       Kellogg Company
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">
       Costco
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Achievement" title="Academy of Achievement">
       Academy of Achievement
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boards_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Boards-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is an
      <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">
       emeritus
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">
       fellow
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Yale_Corporation" title="Yale Corporation">
       Yale Corporation
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boards_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Boards-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 2013, Carson announced he would retire as a surgeon, stating "I'd much rather quit when I'm at the top of my game".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His retirement became official on July 1, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As is normal during medical and academic careers, Dr. Carson participated and cooperated with a variety of professionals in research. They organized their findings into journal articles published in peer-reviewed professional journals. A sample of journals that published his works:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Critical_Care_Medicine_(journal)" title="Critical Care Medicine (journal)">
         Critical Care Medicine (journal)
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
         <a href="#cite_note-28">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          28
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Neuro-Oncology" title="Journal of Neuro-Oncology">
         Journal of Neuro-Oncology
        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         29
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Neurosurgery" title="Journal of Neurosurgery">
         Journal of Neurosurgery
        </a>
       </i>
       , Official Journal of the AANS since 1944.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         <span>
          [
         </span>

         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">
         Neurosurgery
        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         <span>
          [
         </span>

         <span>

         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Human_Pathology" title="Human Pathology">

        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">
       Awards and honors
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Carson is a member of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Achievement" title="American Academy of Achievement">
       American Academy of Achievement
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omega_Alpha" title="Alpha Omega Alpha">
       Alpha Omega Alpha
      </a>
      Honor Medical Society
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Alger_Association_of_Distinguished_Americans" title="Horatio Alger Association of Distinguished Americans">
       Horatio Alger Association of Distinguished Americans
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carson has been awarded 38 honorary doctorate degrees and dozens of national merit citations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Public_Schools" title="Detroit Public Schools">
       Detroit Public Schools
      </a>
      opened the Dr. Benjamin Carson High School of Science and Medicine
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for students interested in pursuing healthcare careers. The school is partnering with
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Receiving_Hospital" title="Detroit Receiving Hospital">
       Detroit Receiving Hospital
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">
       Michigan State University
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In 2000, he received the Award for Greatest Public Service Benefiting the Disadvantaged, an award given out annually by
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service" title="Jefferson Awards for Public Service">
        Jefferson Awards
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         39
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2001, he was elected by the
       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
        Library of Congress
       </a>
       on the occasion of its 200th anniversary to be one of the 89 who earned the designation
       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress_Living_Legend" title="Library of Congress Living Legend">
        Library of Congress Living Legend
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         40
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>

       <a href="/wiki/The_President%27s_Council_on_Bioethics" title="The President's Council on Bioethics">
        The President's Council on Bioethics
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         41
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>

       <a href="/wiki/William_E._Simon_Prize_for_Philanthropic_Leadership" title="William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership">
        William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership
       </a>
       .

         </span>

         <span>

         </span>

       </sup>
      </li>

       </a>
       from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">

       </a>

       </a>

       </a>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Writer">
       Writer
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Carson has written six
      <a href="/wiki/Bestseller" title="Bestseller">
       bestselling
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      books published by
      <a href="/wiki/Zondervan" title="Zondervan">
       Zondervan
      </a>
      , an international Christian media and publishing company. The first book is an
      <a href="/wiki/Autobiography" title="Autobiography">
       autobiography
      </a>
      , and two are about his personal philosophies of success (hard work, faith). Here are his books in English and Spanish editions:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        Gifted Hands: The Ben Carson Story
       </i>
       This book was released by
       <a href="/wiki/Zondervan" title="Zondervan">
        Zondervan
       </a>
       in 1992.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         52
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       A separate
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_movie" title="Television movie">
        television movie
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Gifted_Hands:_The_Ben_Carson_Story" title="Gifted Hands: The Ben Carson Story">
        same title
       </a>
       premiered on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turner_Network_Television" title="Turner Network Television">
        TNT
       </a>
       on February 7, 2009, with Academy Award winner
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuba_Gooding_Jr." title="Cuba Gooding Jr.">
        Cuba Gooding Jr.
       </a>
       in the lead role and
       <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Elise" title="Kimberly Elise">
        Kimberly Elise
       </a>
       portraying his mother.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         53
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Manos Prodigiosas: La historia de Ben Carson
       </i>
       (Spanish Edition)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         54
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       is published by Vida.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Corre el Riesgo: Aprenda a identificar, elegir, y vivir, con un riesgo moderado
       </i>
       (Spanish Edition)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">

          [
         </span>

         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Piense en Grande: Libera tu potencial de excelencia!
       </i>
       (Spanish Edition)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">

         <span>
          [
         </span>
         56
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Think Big: Unleashing Your Potential for Excellence
       </i>
       is his follow-up to
       <i>
        Gifted Hands
       </i>
       and prescribes his personal formula for success.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         <span>
          [
         </span>

         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Big Picture: Getting Perspective on What's Really Important in Life
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         58
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       shares Dr. Carson's overarching philosophy that has shaped his life.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Take the Risk: Learning to Identify, Choose, and Live with Acceptable Risk
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">

          [
         </span>
         59
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       reveals insights that will help dispel fear of risk in order to dream big, aim high, move with confidence, and reap unimagined rewards.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        America the Beautiful: Rediscovering What Made This Nation Great
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">

          [
         </span>

         <span>

         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       helps us learn from our past in order to chart a better course for our future.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        One Nation: What We Can All Do to Save America's Future
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         61
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        One Nation
       </i>
       in particular was a massive success, remaining at the top of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times_Best-Seller" title="New York Times Best-Seller">
        <i>
         New York Times
        </i>
        bestsellers
       </a>
       list for 20 straight weeks, with 5 weeks as #1, outselling
       <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">
        Hillary Clinton
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hard_Choices" title="Hard Choices">
         Hard Choices
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes1_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Barnes1-62">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         62
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        You Have a Brain: A Teen's Guide to T.H.I.N.K. B.I.G.
       </i>
       , outlining eight principles that helped shape Dr. Carson's future.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         63
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        One Vote: Make Your Voice Heard
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">

         <span>
          [
         </span>
         64
         <span>
          ]

       </sup>
       explains how to discover the true power of the ballot.
      </li>

       <i>
        My Life: Based on the Book Gifted Hands
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         65
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       contains a new chapter about Dr. Carson's philosophies of serving one's country, becoming a role model, and other characteristics that lead to success in life while being a benefit to others.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      On July 8, 2013, Carson joined
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Times" title="The Washington Times">
        The Washington Times
       </a>
      </i>
      as a weekly opinion columnist. He also writes for
      <i>
       American CurrentSee
      </i>
      , an online publication for conservative African-Americans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_affiliation_and_views">
       Political affiliation and views
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Carson had said he was not a member of any
      <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">
       political party
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NR_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NR-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, he joined the
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican Party
      </a>
      on November 4, 2014, the day the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_midterms" title="2014 midterms">
       2014 midterms
      </a>
      took place, as "truly a pragmatic move" because he was considering running for
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">
       president in 2016
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In his book
      <i>
       America the Beautiful
      </i>
      , he explained his decision to enter politics: "I believe it is a very good idea for physicians, scientists, engineers, and others trained to make decisions based on facts and empirical data to get involved in the political arena".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_health_insurance_companies">
       Criticism of health insurance companies
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In a 1996 interview, Carson said that he found the "concept of for profits for the insurance companies" absurd. He continued, "The first thing we need to do is get rid of for-profit insurance companies. We have a lack of policies and we need to make the government responsible for catastrophic health care".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanthinker.com_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-americanthinker.com-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014 Carson wrote, ". . . we need to remove health care from the political arena and recognize that any government proposals affecting the health of all citizens should be free market-based and should be so appealing that it would not be necessary to force citizens into the program."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="End-of-life_care">
       End-of-life care
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1992, Carson wrote that aging and technological advancement will eventually lead to many people surviving their 100th birthdays. He questioned the merits of prolonging life, citing the fact that "up to half of the medical expenses incurred in the average American's life are incurred during the last six months of life". He discussed the "dignity of dying in comfort, at home, with an attendant if necessary" and stated, "Decisions on who should be treated and who should not be treated would clearly require some national guidelines".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanthinker.com_71-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-americanthinker.com-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In January 2015, Carson countered that his views have evolved since then.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="National_Prayer_Breakfast_speech_on_social_and_fiscal_issues">
       National Prayer Breakfast speech on social and fiscal issues
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Carson was the keynote speaker at the February 7, 2013
      <a href="/wiki/National_Prayer_Breakfast" title="National Prayer Breakfast">
       National Prayer Breakfast
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In his speech, he commented on
      <a href="/wiki/Political_correctness" title="Political correctness">
       political correctness
      </a>
      ("dangerous", because it goes against
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" title="Freedom of expression">
       freedom of expression
      </a>
      ), education, health care, and taxation. Regarding education, he spoke favorably about graduation rates in 1831, when
      <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville" title="Alexis de Tocqueville">
       Alexis de Tocqueville
      </a>
      visited the United States, and when "anybody finishing the second grade was completely literate". He espoused the idea of a tax-exempt
      <a href="/wiki/Health_savings_account" title="Health savings account">
       health savings account
      </a>
      created at birth, that can be bequeathed at death, along with an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_medical_record" title="Electronic medical record">
       electronic medical record
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">
       birth certificate
      </a>
      . He supports a
      <a href="/wiki/Flat_tax" title="Flat tax">
       flat tax
      </a>
      , which he calls the "proportional tax" in reference to the
      <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">
       biblical
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">
       tithe
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The speech was magnified because Carson's views were generally interpreted to be
      <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">
       politically conservative
      </a>
      , and President
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      was sitting just feet away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Conservative commentators from
      <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">
       Rush Limbaugh
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Sean_Hannity" title="Sean Hannity">
       Sean Hannity
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Cavuto" title="Neil Cavuto">
       Neil Cavuto
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">
       Fox News
      </a>
      praised the speech as an example of speaking "truth to power".
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">
        The Wall Street Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      titled one of its
      <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">
       op-eds
      </a>
      "Ben Carson for President".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Columnist
      <a href="/wiki/Star_Parker" title="Star Parker">
       Star Parker
      </a>
      wrote that he "owes no apology for honest talk".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fox contributor Cal Thomas and commentator Bob Beckel, however, found his comments inappropriate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_(cropped).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="202" data-file-width="198" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Ben_Carson_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="198"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        At White House in 2008 for award
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In an interview with Neil Cavuto, Carson defended himself, "Somebody has to be courageous enough to stand up to the bullies".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 8, he appeared on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Hannity" title="Hannity">
        Hannity
       </a>
      </i>
      , and said that he would run for president "If the Lord grabbed me by the collar and made me do it".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the speech, Carson said: "I don't think it was particularly political...You know, I'm a physician".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rea_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rea-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Regarding the policies of President Obama, he said: "There are a number of policies that I don't believe lead to the growth of our nation and don't lead to the elevation of our nation. I don't want to sit here and say all of his policies are bad. What I would like to see more often in this nation is an open and intelligent conversation".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rea_86-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rea-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Review" title="National Review">
        National Review
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Goldberg" title="Jonah Goldberg">
       Jonah Goldberg
      </a>
      compared Carson to
      <a href="/wiki/Booker_T._Washington" title="Booker T. Washington">
       Booker T. Washington
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while David Graham compared him to
      <a href="/wiki/Herman_Cain" title="Herman Cain">
       Herman Cain
      </a>
      without the "personal skeletons" in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">
        The Atlantic
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson's sudden popularity among conservatives led to him being invited as a featured speaker at the 2013
      <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Political_Action_Conference" title="Conservative Political Action Conference">
       Conservative Political Action Conference
      </a>
      (CPAC). He tied for seventh place in the
      <i>
       Washington Times
      </i>
      /CPAC 2013
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Straw_Poll" title="Straw Poll">
       Straw Poll
      </a>
      with 4% of the 3,000 ballots cast.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the 2014 CPAC straw poll, he came in third place with 9% of the vote, behind
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
       senators
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Ted_Cruz" title="Ted Cruz">
       Ted Cruz
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
       Texas
      </a>
      (with 11%) and
      <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">
       Rand Paul
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">
       Kentucky
      </a>
      (31%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson had a strong showing in the polls at the 2013 and 2014
      <a href="/wiki/Values_Voter_Summit" title="Values Voter Summit">
       Values Voter Summits
      </a>
      : in 2013, he tied with former
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
       Pennsylvania
      </a>
      senator
      <a href="/wiki/Rick_Santorum" title="Rick Santorum">
       Rick Santorum
      </a>
      for second place with 13%, behind Ted Cruz's 42%. In 2014, he took 20% of the Values Voter Summit vote to Cruz's 25% and came in first place for the vice presidential poll.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_homosexuality">
       Marriage and homosexuality
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In March 2013, Carson described his views about
      <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">
       same-sex marriage
      </a>
      on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Hannity" title="Hannity">
        Hannity
       </a>
      </i>
      , saying: "Marriage is between a man and a woman. No group, be they gays, be they
      <a href="/wiki/North_American_Man/Boy_Love_Association" title="North American Man/Boy Love Association">
       NAMBLA
      </a>
      , be they people who believe in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bestiality" title="Bestiality">
       bestiality
      </a>
      , it doesn't matter what they are. They don't get to change the definition."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politico-remark_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-politico-remark-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carson's comments drew criticism for using "gays" in the same sentence as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedophiles" title="Pedophiles">
       pedophiles
      </a>
      and practitioners of bestiality. A group of
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">
       Hopkins
      </a>
      students petitioned that he be replaced as the university's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commencement_speaker" title="Commencement speaker">
       commencement speaker
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politico-remark_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-politico-remark-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun-withdraw_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sun-withdraw-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Several days later, Carson withdrew as Hopkins's commencement speaker and apologized, saying that "the examples were not the best choice of words", adding that the
      <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">
       Bible
      </a>
      "says we have an obligation to love our fellow man as ourselves, and I love everybody the sameall homosexuals".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun-withdraw_95-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sun-withdraw-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-withdraw_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-post-withdraw-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He said on
      <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
       CNN
      </a>
      that he loved all people, whether gay or straight.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politico-remark_94-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-politico-remark-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carson added, "I was trying to say that as far as marriage was concerned, it has traditionally been between a man and a woman and no one should be able to change that."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insider_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-insider-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In October 2014, Carson was added to the
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_Poverty_Law_Center" title="Southern Poverty Law Center">
       Southern Poverty Law Center
      </a>
      (SPLC)'s extremist watch list because of his association with groups considered by SPLC to be extremist in nature, "linking gays with pedophiles", and his comparison of health care and liberal government to slavery and
      <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">
       totalitarianism
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chasmar_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chasmar-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wong_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wong-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In February 2015, the SPLC removed his name and apologized to Dr. Carson,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      stating: "In October 2014, we posted an 'Extremist File' of Dr. Ben Carson. This week, as we've come under intense criticism for doing so, we've reviewed our profile and have concluded that it did not meet our standards, so we have taken it down and apologize to Dr. Carson for having posted it. We've also come to the conclusion that the question of whether a better-researched profile of Dr. Carson should or should not be included in our 'Extremist Files' is taking attention from the fact that Dr. Carson has, in fact, made a number of statements that express views that we believe most people would conclude are extreme."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a March 2015 interview with
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_Cuomo" title="Chris Cuomo">
       Chris Cuomo
      </a>
      , Carson stated that
      <a href="/wiki/Biology_and_sexual_orientation" title="Biology and sexual orientation">
       homosexuality
      </a>
      was "absolutely" a choice, claiming that "a lot of people go into
      <a href="/wiki/Prison_sexuality" title="Prison sexuality">
       prison straight
      </a>
      , and when they come out, they're gay".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a
      <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">
       Facebook
      </a>
      post, Carson apologized, saying that he "[does] not pretend to know how every individual came to their sexual orientation."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a Facebook post, Carson said that he supports
      <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">
       civil unions
      </a>
      for gay couples and that he has "for many years".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">
       Evolution
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Carson's views on
      <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">
       evolution
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Creationism" title="Creationism">
       creationism
      </a>
      have also been controversial.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPevolution_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WPevolution-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2006 debate with
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dawkins" title="Richard Dawkins">
       Richard Dawkins
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_Collins_(geneticist)" title="Francis Collins (geneticist)">
       Francis Collins
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Dennett" title="Daniel Dennett">
       Daniel Dennett
      </a>
      , Carson stated: "I don't believe in evolution...I simply don't have enough faith to believe that something as complex as our ability to rationalize, think, and plan, and have a moral sense of what's right and wrong, just appeared."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2012, nearly 500 professors, students, and alumni of
      <a href="/wiki/Emory_University" title="Emory University">
       Emory University
      </a>
      wrote a letter expressing concern about his views in advance of his commencement speech (there was no request to rescind the invitation). They cited a quote in an interview with the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Adventist_Review" title="Adventist Review">
        Adventist Review
       </a>
      </i>
      : "By believing we are the product of random acts, we eliminate morality and the basis of ethical behavior". Carson clarified that "Those of us who believe in God and derive our sense of right and wrong and ethics from God's word really have no difficulty whatsoever defining where our ethics come from. People who believe in survival of the fittest might have more difficulty deriving where their ethics come from. A lot of evolutionists are very ethical people."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPevolution_111-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WPevolution-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Affordable_Care_Act">
       Affordable Care Act
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On October 11, 2013, Carson spoke at the conservative
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Values_Voters_Summit" title="Values Voters Summit">
       Values Voters Summit
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
       Washington, D.C.
      </a>
      , where he called the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Affordable_Care_Act" title="Affordable Care Act">
       Affordable Care Act
      </a>
      (ACA) "the worst thing that has happened in this nation since
      <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">
       slavery
      </a>
      ". He claimed that the ACA originated with
      <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">
       Vladimir Lenin
      </a>
      , and quoted Lenin as saying that "socialized medicine is the keystone to the establishment of a
      <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">
       socialist state
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There is no evidence that Lenin actually said this, but the purported quote appears on a number of conservative websites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lenin_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lenin-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heart-of-power_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-heart-of-power-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After an onslaught of criticism, Carson denied that he was "equating Obamacare with slavery" in an October 15
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Times" title="Washington Times">
        Washington Times
       </a>
      </i>
      column and denounced the "
      <a href="/wiki/Political_correctness" title="Political correctness">
       PC
      </a>
      police" for attempting "to discredit and...silence" him.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During the National Prayer Breakfast, Carson said about the ACA:
      <i>
       Here's my solution. When a person is born, give him a birth certificate, an electronic medical record and a
       <a href="/wiki/Health_savings_account" title="Health savings account">
        health savings account
       </a>
       [HSA]."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         117
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </i>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cannabis_legalization">
       Cannabis legalization
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Carson is against the legalization of recreational
      <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">
       cannabis
      </a>
      . He believes it to be a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gateway_drug" title="Gateway drug">
       gateway drug
      </a>
      that leads to "hedonistic activity".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Gun_control">
       Gun control
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Carson stated in a 2013 interview with
      <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Beck" title="Glenn Beck">
       Glenn Beck
      </a>
      that
      <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_firearm" title="Semi-automatic firearm">
       semi-automatic firearms
      </a>
      should be better regulated in large cities and high-crime areas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This statement has caused some with conservative views on gun control to question if his views were at odds with most conservatives. Later, clarifying that "This isnt any evolution of my views, just that Ive learned how to express myself," he stated that he is strongly in favor of the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Second Amendment to the United States Constitution">
       Second Amendment
      </a>
      and that while guns being used on innocent people "is horrible," it "is not nearly as horrible as having a population that is defenseless against a group of tyrants who have arms. And that is what we have to bear in mind."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also said that if in a position of national authority, he would allow citizens to own any weapons, including automatic and semi-automatic guns, that they could buy
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and that he would not support any efforts to restrict the Second Amendment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Presidential_campaign">
       2016 Presidential campaign
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Ben_Carson_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Ben Carson presidential campaign, 2016">
       Ben Carson presidential campaign, 2016
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In January 2015,
      <i>
       The Weekly Standard
      </i>
      reported that the Draft Carson Committee had raised $13 million by the end of 2014, shortly after Carson performed well in a
      <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
       CNN
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/ORC_International" title="ORC International">
       ORC
      </a>
      poll of potential candidates in December 2014, coming in second in two different versions. He came in second with 10% behind Mitt Romney's 20%, but in the same poll with Romney removed from the list, Carson closed the gap with 11% to Jeb Bush's 14%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes1_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barnes1-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" title="Wall Street Journal">
        Wall Street Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      mentioned that the Draft Carson Committee had chairmen in all of
      <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">
       Iowa
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Iowa" title="List of counties in Iowa">
       99 counties
      </a>
      , and that Carson had recently come in first place in two separate
      <a href="/wiki/Public_Policy_Polling" title="Public Policy Polling">
       Public Policy polls
      </a>
      for the state of
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
       Pennsylvania
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On May 3, 2015, Carson confirmed his candidacy for President in an interview with a local television station in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">
       Cincinnati, Ohio
      </a>
      . He officially announced he was running for the
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2016">
       Republican nomination
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">
       2016 Presidential election
      </a>
      at a rally in
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">
       Detroit
      </a>
      , his hometown, on May 4, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Carson_Scholars_Fund">
       Carson Scholars Fund
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In 1994, Carson and his wife started the Carson Scholars Fund, which gave scholarships to students in grades 411 for "academic excellence and humanitarian qualities".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSF_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CSF-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They founded it after reading that U.S. students ranked second to last in terms of math and science testing among 22 countries. They also noticed that schools awarded athletes with trophies whereas honor students only received "a pin or certificate".
     </p>
     <p>
      Recipients of the Carson Scholars Fund get a $1,000 scholarship towards their college education. It has awarded 6,700 scholarships.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSF_129-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CSF-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In recognition for his work with the Carson Scholars Fund and other charitable giving throughout his lifetime, Carson was awarded the William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership in 2005.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">
       Personal life
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Carson and his wife, Lacena "Candy" Rustin, met in 1971 as students at
      <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">
       Yale University
      </a>
      . They married in 1975 and have three sons: Murray, Benjamin Jr., and Rhoeyce. They live in
      <a href="/wiki/West_Friendship,_Maryland" title="West Friendship, Maryland">
       West Friendship
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">
       Maryland
      </a>
      , and are members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">
       Seventh-day Adventist Church
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notable_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-notable-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Carson was baptized at Burns Seventh-day Adventist Church on Detroit's eastside. A few years later he told the pastor at a church in
      <a href="/wiki/Inkster,_Michigan" title="Inkster, Michigan">
       Inkster, Michigan
      </a>
      he was attending that he had not fully understood his first baptism and wanted to be baptized again, so he was. He has served as a local elder and Sabbath school teacher in the Seventh-day Adventist Church.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His mother is a devout Seventh-day Adventist.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

         Tsuchida, T., Hruban, R. H., Carson, B. S., &amp; Phillips, P. C. (1992). Colloid cysts of the third ventricle: immunohistochemical evidence for nonneuroepithelial differentiation. Human pathology, 23(7), 811-816.
